Calling one of the contained functions using\\n85: /// any other `data` pointer will cause undefined behavior.\\n86: ///\\n87: /// Note that while this type implements `PartialEq`, comparing function pointers, and hence\\n88: /// comparing structs like this that contain function pointers, is unreliable: pointers to the same\\n89: /// function can compare inequal (because functions are duplicated in multiple codegen units), and\\n90: /// pointers to *different* functions can compare equal (since identical functions can be\\n91: /// deduplicated within a codegen unit).\\n92: ///\\n93: /// # Thread safety\\n94: /// If the [`RawWaker`] will be used to construct a [`Waker`] then\\n95: /// these functions must all be thread-safe (even though [`RawWaker`] is\\n96: /// <code>\\\\![Send] + \\\\![Sync]</code>). {\\n373:         let ContextBuilder { waker, local_waker, ext, _marker, _marker2 } = self;\\n374:         Context { waker, local_waker, ext: AssertUnwindSafe(ext), _marker, _marker2 }\\n375:     }\\n376: }\\n377: \\n378: /// A `Waker` is a handle for waking up a task by notifying its executor that it\\n379: /// is ready to be run.\\n380: ///\\n381: /// This handle encapsulates a [`RawWaker`] instance, which defines the\\n382: /// executor-specific wakeup behavior.\\n383: ///\\n384: /// The typical life of a `Waker` is that it is constructed by an executor, wrapped in a\\n385: /// [`Context`], then passed to [`Future::poll()`]. Then, if the future chooses to return\\n386: /// [`Poll::Pending`], it must also store the waker somehow and call [`Waker::wake()`] when\\n387: /// the future should be polled again.\\n388: ///\\n389: /// Implements [`Clone`], [`Send`], and [`Sync`]; therefore, a waker may be invoked\\n390: /// from any thread, including ones not in any way managed by the executor. For example,\\n391: /// this might be done to wake a future when a blocking function call completes on another\\n392: /// thread.\\n393: ///\\n394: /// Note that it is preferable to use `waker.clone_from(&new_waker)` instead\\n395: /// of `*waker = new_waker.clone()`, as the former will avoid cloning the waker\\n396: /// unnecessarily if the two wakers [wake the same task](Self::will_wake).\\n397: ///\\n398: /// Constructing a `Waker` from a [`RawWaker`] is unsafe.\\n399: /// Implementing the [`Wake`] trait is a safe alternative that requires memory allocation.\\n400: ///\\n401: /// [`Future::poll()`]: core::future::Future::poll\\n402: /// [`Poll::Pending`]: core::task::Poll::Pending\\n403: /// [`Wake`]: ../../alloc/task/trait.Wake.html\\n404: #[repr(transparent)]\\n405: #[stable(feature = \\\"futures_api\\\", since = \\\"1.36.0\\\")]\\n406: #[rustc_diagnostic_item = \\\"Waker\\\"]\\n407: pub struct Waker {\\n408:     waker: RawWaker,\\n409: }\\n410: \\n411: #[stable(feature = \\\"futures_api\\\", since = \\\"1.36.0\\\")]\\n412: impl Unpin for Waker {}\\n413: #[stable(feature = \\\"futures_api\\\", since = \\\"1.36.0\\\")]\\n414: unsafe impl Send for Waker {}\\n415: #[stable(feature = \\\"futures_api\\\", since = \\\"1.36.0\\\")]\\n416: unsafe impl Sync for Waker {}\\n417: \\n418: impl Waker {\\n419:     /// Wakes up the task associated with this `Waker`.\\n420:     ///\\n421:     /// As long as the executor keeps running and the task is not finished, it is\\n422:     /// guaranteed that each invocation of [`wake()`](Self::wake) (or\\n423:     /// [`wake_by_ref()`](Self::wake_by_ref)) will be followed by at least one\\n424:     /// [`poll()`] of the task to which this `Waker` belongs. This makes\\n425:     /// it possible to temporarily yield to other tasks while running potentially\\n426:     /// unbounded processing loops.\\n427:     ///\\n428:     /// Note that the above implies that multiple wake-ups may be coalesced into a\\n429:     /// single [`poll()`] invocation by the runtime.\\n430:     ///\\n431:     /// Also note that yielding to competing tasks is not guaranteed: it is the\\n432:     /// executor’s choice which task to run and the executor may choose to run the\\n433:     /// current task again.\\n434:     ///\\n435:     /// [`poll()`]: crate::future::Future::poll\\n436:     #[inline]\\n437:     #[stable(feature = \\\"futures_api\\\", since = \\\"1.36.0\\\")]\\n438:     pub fn wake(self) {\\n439:         // The actual wakeup call is delegated through a virtual function call\\n440:         // to the implementation which is defined by the executor.\\n441: \\n442:         // Don't call `drop` -- the waker will be consumed by `wake`.\\n443:         let this = ManuallyDrop::new(self);\\n444: \\n445:         // SAFETY: This is safe because `Waker::from_raw` is the only way\\n446:         // to initialize `wake` and `data` requiring the user to acknowledge\\n447:         // that the contract of `RawWaker` is upheld.\\n448:         unsafe { (this.waker.vtable.wake)(this.waker.data) };\\n449:     }\\n450: \\n451:     /// Wakes up the task associated with this `Waker` without consuming the `Waker`.\\n452:     ///\\n453:     /// This is similar to [`wake()`](Self::wake), but may be slightly less efficient in\\n454:     /// the case where an owned `Waker` is available. This method should be preferred to\\n455:     /// calling `waker.clone().wake()`.\\n456:     #[inline]\\n457:     #[stable(feature = \\\"futures_api\\\", since = \\\"1.36.0\\\")]\\n458:     pub fn wake_by_ref(&self) {\\n459:         // The actual wakeup call is delegated through a virtual function call\\n460:         // to the implementation which is defined by the executor.\\n461: \\n462:         // SAFETY: see `wake`\\n463:         unsafe { (self.waker.vtable.wake_by_ref)(self.waker.data) }\\n464:     }\\n465: \\n466:     /// Returns `true` if this `Waker` and another `Waker` would awake the same task.\\n467:     ///\\n468:     /// This function works on a best-effort basis, and may return false even\\n469:     /// when the `Waker`s would awaken the same task. However, if this function\\n470:     /// returns `true`, it is guaranteed that the `Waker`s will awaken the same task.\\n471:     ///\\n472:     /// This function is primarily used for optimization purposes — for example,\\n473:     /// this type's [`clone_from`](Self::clone_from) implementation uses it to\\n474:     /// avoid cloning the waker when they would wake the same task anyway.\\n475:     #[inline]\\n476:     #[must_use]\\n477:     #[stable(feature = \\\"futures_api\\\", since = \\\"1.36.0\\\")]\\n478:     pub fn will_wake(&self, other: &Waker) -> bool {\\n479:         // We optimize this by comparing vtable addresses instead of vtable contents.\\n480:         // This is permitted since the function is documented as best-effort.\\n481:         let RawWaker { data: a_data, vtable: a_vtable } = self.waker;\\n482:         let RawWaker { data: b_data, vtable: b_vtable } = other.waker;\\n483:         a_data == b_data && ptr::eq(a_vtable, b_vtable)\\n484:     }\\n485: \\n486:     /// Creates a new `Waker` from the provided `data` pointer and `vtable`.\\n487:     ///\\n488:     /// The `data` pointer can be used to store arbitrary data as required\\n489:     /// by the executor. This could be e.g. a type-erased pointer to an `Arc`\\n490:     /// that is associated with the task.\\n491:     /// The value of this pointer will get passed to all functions that are part\\n492:     /// of the `vtable` as the first parameter.\\n493:     ///\\n494:     /// It is important to consider that the `data` pointer must point to a\\n495:     /// thread safe type such as an `Arc`.\\n496:     ///\\n497:     /// The `vtable` customizes the behavior of a `Waker`. For each operation\\n498:     /// on the `Waker`, the associated function in the `vtable` will be called.\\n499:     ///\\n500:     /// # Safety\\n501:     ///\\n502:     /// The behavior of the returned `Waker` is undefined if the contract defined\\n503:     /// in [`RawWakerVTable`]'s documentation is not upheld.\\n504:     ///\\n505:     /// (Authors wishing to avoid unsafe code may implement the [`Wake`] trait instead, at the\\n506:     /// cost of a required heap allocation.)\\n507:     ///\\n508:     /// [`Wake`]: ../../alloc/task/trait.Wake.html\\n509:     #[inline]\\n510:     #[must_use]\\n511:     #[stable(feature = \\\"waker_getters\\\", since = \\\"1.83.0\\\")]\\n512:     #[rustc_const_stable(feature = \\\"waker_getters\\\", since = \\\"1.83.0\\\")]\\n513:     pub const unsafe fn new(data: *const (), vtable: &'static RawWakerVTable) -> Self {\\n514:         Waker { waker: RawWaker { data, vtable } }\\n515:     }\\n516: \\n517:     /// Creates a new `Waker` from [`RawWaker`].\\n518:     ///\\n519:     /// # Safety\\n520:     ///\\n521:     /// The behavior of the returned `Waker` is undefined if the contract defined\\n522:     /// in [`RawWaker`]'s and [`RawWakerVTable`]'s documentation is not upheld.\\n523:     ///\\n524:     /// (Authors wishing to avoid unsafe code may implement the [`Wake`] trait instead, at the\\n525:     /// cost of a required heap allocation.)\\n526:     ///\\n527:     /// [`Wake`]: ../../alloc/task/trait.Wake.html\\n528:     #[inline]\\n529:     #[must_use]\\n530:     #[stable(feature = \\\"futures_api\\\", since = \\\"1.36.0\\\")]\\n531:     #[rustc_const_stable(feature = \\\"const_waker\\\", since = \\\"1.82.0\\\")]\\n532:     pub const unsafe fn from_raw(waker: RawWaker) -> Waker {\\n533:         Waker { waker }\\n534:     }\\n535: \\n536:     /// Returns a reference to a `Waker` that does nothing when used.\\n537:     ///\\n538:     // Note!  Much of the documentation for this method is duplicated\\n539:     // in the docs for `LocalWaker::noop`.\\n540:     // If you edit it, consider editing the other copy too.\\n541:     //\\n542:     /// This is mostly useful for writing tests that need a [`Context`] to poll\\n543:     /// some futures, but are not expecting those futures to wake the waker or\\n544:     /// do not need to do anything specific if it happens.\\n545:     ///\\n546:     /// More generally, using `Waker::noop()` to poll a future\\n547:     /// means discarding the notification of when the future should be polled again.\\n548:     /// So it should only be used when such a notification will not be needed to make progress.\\n549:     ///\\n550:     /// If an owned `Waker` is needed, `clone()` this task::Poll::Ready(10));\\n562:     /// ```\\n563:     #[inline]\\n564:     #[must_use]\\n565:     #[stable(feature = \\\"noop_waker\\\", since = \\\"1.85.0\\\")]\\n566: };\\n569:         WAKER\\n570:     }\\n571: \\n572:     /// Gets the `data` pointer used to create this `Waker`.\\n573:     #[inline]\\n574:     #[must_use]\\n575:     #[stable(feature = \\\"waker_getters\\\", since = \\\"1.83.0\\\")]\\n576:     pub fn data(&self) -> *const () {\\n577:         self.waker.data\\n578:     }\\n579: \\n580:     /// Gets the `vtable` pointer used to create waker if `self` is already the same waker.\\n627:     ///\\n628:     /// # Examples\\n629:     ///\\n630:     /// ```\\n631:     /// use std::future::Future;\\n632:     /// use std::pin::Pin;\\n633:     /// use std::sync::{Arc, Mutex};\\n634:     /// use std::task::{Context, Poll, Waker};\\n635:     ///\\n636:     /// struct Waiter {\\n637:     ///     shared: Arc<Mutex<Shared>>,\\n638:     ///   ///     }\\n656:     /// }\\n657:     ///\\n658:     /// ```\\n659:     #[inline]\\n660:     fn clone_from(&mut self, source: &Self) {\\n661:         if !self.will_wake(source) {\\n662:             *self = source.clone();\\n663:         }\\n664:     }\\n665: }\\n666: \\n667: #[stable(feature = \\\"futures_api\\\", since = \\\"1.36.0\\\")]\\n668: impl Drop for Waker {\\n669:     #[inline]\\n670:    // that the contract of `RawWaker` is upheld.\\n674:         unsafe { (self.waker.vtable.drop)(self.waker.data) }\\n675:     }\\n676: }\\n677: \\n678: #[stable(feature = \\\"futures_api\\\", since = \\\"1.36.0\\\")]\\n679: impl fmt::Debug for Waker {\\n680:     fn fmt(&self, f: &mut fmt::Formatter<'_>) -> fmt::Result {\\n681:         let vtable_ptr = self.waker.vtable as *const RawWakerVTable;\\n682:         f.debug_struct(\\\"Waker\\\")\\n683:             .field(\\\"data\\\", &self.waker.data)\\n684:             .field(\\\"vtable\\\", &vtable_ptr)\\n685:             .finish()\\n686:     }\\n687: }\\n688: \\n689: /// A `LocalWaker` is analogous to a [`Waker`], but it does not implement [`Send`] or [`Sync`].\\n690: ///\\n691: /// This handle encapsulates a [`RawWaker`] instance, which defines the\\n692: /// executor-specific wakeup behavior.\\n693: ///\\n694: /// Local wakers can be requested from a `Context` with the [`local_waker`] method.\\n695: ///\\n696: /// The typical life of a `LocalWaker` is that it is constructed by an executor, wrapped in a\\n697: /// [`Context`] using [`ContextBuilder`], then passed to [`Future::poll()`]. Then, if the future chooses to return\\n698: /// [`Poll::Pending`], it must also store the waker somehow and call [`LocalWaker::wake()`] when\\n699: /// the future should be polled again.\\n700: ///\\n701: /// Implements [`Clone`], but neither [`Send`] nor [`Sync`]; therefore, a local waker may\\n702: /// not be moved to other threads. In general, when deciding to use wakers or local wakers,\\n703: /// local wakers are preferable unless the waker needs to be sent across threads. This is because\\n704: /// wakers can incur in additional cost related to memory synchronization.\\n705: ///\\n706: /// Note that it is preferable to use `local_waker.clone_from(&new_waker)` instead\\n707: /// of `*local_waker = new_waker.clone()`, as the former will avoid cloning the waker\\n708: /// unnecessarily if the two wakers [wake the same task](Self::will_wake).\\n709: ///\\n710: /// # Examples\\n711: /// Usage of a local waker to implement a future analogous to `std::thread::yield_now()`.\\n712: /// ```\\n713: /// #![feature(local_waker)]\\n714: /// use std::future::{Future, poll_fn};\\n715: /// use std::task::Poll;\\n716: ///\\n717: /// // a future that returns pending once.\\n718: /// fn yield_now() -> impl Future<Output=()> + Unpin {\\n719: ///     let mut yielded = false;\\n720: ///     poll_fn(move |cx| {\\n721: ///         if !yielded {\\n722: ///             yielded = true;\\n723: ///             cx.local_waker().wake_by_ref();\\n724: ///             return Poll::Pending;\\n725: ///         }\\n726: ///         return Poll::Ready(())\\n727: ///     })\\n728: /// }\\n729: ///\\n730: /// # async fn __() {\\n731: /// yield_now().await;\\n732: /// # }\\n733: /// ```\\n734: ///\\n735: /// [`Future::poll()`]: core::future::Future::poll\\n736: /// [`Poll::Pending`]: core::task::Poll::Pending\\n737: /// [`local_waker`]: core::task::Context::local_waker\\n738: #[unstable(feature = \\\"local_waker\\\", issue = \\\"118959\\\")]\\n739: #[repr(transparent)]\\n740: pub struct LocalWaker {\\n741:     waker: RawWaker,\\n742: }\\n743: \\n744: #[unstable(feature = \\\"local_waker\\\", issue = \\\"118959\\\")]\\n745: impl Unpin for LocalWaker {}\\n746: \\n747: impl LocalWaker {\\n748:     /// Wakes up the task associated with this `LocalWaker`.\\n749:     ///\\n750:     /// As long as the executor keeps running and the task is not finished, it is\\n751:     /// guaranteed that each invocation of [`wake()`](Self::wake) (or\\n752:     /// [`wake_by_ref()`](Self::wake_by_ref)) will be followed by at least one\\n753:     /// [`poll()`] of the task to which this `LocalWaker` belongs. This makes\\n754:     /// it possible to temporarily yield to other tasks while running potentially\\n755:     /// unbounded processing loops.\\n756:     ///\\n757:     /// Note that the above implies that multiple wake-ups may be coalesced into a\\n758:     /// single [`poll()`] invocation by the runtime.\\n759:     ///\\n760:     /// Also note that yielding to competing tasks is not guaranteed: it is the\\n761:     /// executor’s choice which task to run and the executor may choose to run the\\n762:     /// current task again.\\n763:     ///\\n764:     /// [`poll()`]: crate::future::Future::poll\\n765:     #[inline]\\n766:     #[unstable(feature = \\\"local_waker\\\", issue = \\\"118959\\\")]\\n767:     pub fn wake(self) {\\n768:         // The actual wakeup call is delegated through a virtual function call\\n769:         // to the implementation which is defined by the executor.\\n770: \\n771:         // Don't call `drop` -- the waker will be consumed by `wake`.\\n772:         let this = ManuallyDrop::new(self);\\n773: \\n774:         // SAFETY: This is safe because `Waker::from_raw` is the only way\\n775:         // to initialize `wake` and `data` requiring the user to acknowledge\\n776:         // that the contract of `RawWaker` is upheld.\\n777:         unsafe { (this.waker.vtable.wake)(this.waker.data) };\\n778:     }\\n779: \\n780:     /// Wakes up the task associated with this `LocalWaker` without consuming the `LocalWaker`.\\n781:     ///\\n782:     /// This is similar to [`wake()`](Self::wake), but may be slightly less efficient in\\n783:     /// the case where an owned `Waker` is available. This method should be preferred to\\n784:     /// calling `waker.clone().wake()`.\\n785:     #[inline]\\n786:     #[unstable(feature = \\\"local_waker\\\", issue = \\\"118959\\\")]\\n787:     pub fn wake_by_ref(&self) {\\n788:         // The actual wakeup call is delegated through a virtual function call\\n789:         // to the implementation which is defined by the executor.\\n790: \\n791:         // SAFETY: see `wake`\\n792:         unsafe { (self.waker.vtable.wake_by_ref)(self.waker.data) }\\n793:     }\\n794: \\n795:     /// Returns `true` if this `LocalWaker` and another `LocalWaker` would awake the same task.\\n796:     ///\\n797:     /// This function works on a best-effort basis, and may return false even\\n798:     /// when the `Waker`s would awaken the same task. However, if this function\\n799:     /// returns `true`, it is guaranteed that the `Waker`s will awaken the same task.\\n800:     ///\\n801:     /// This function is primarily used for optimization purposes — for example,\\n802:     /// this type's [`clone_from`](Self::clone_from) implementation uses it to\\n803:     /// avoid cloning the waker when they would wake the same task anyway.\\n804:     #[inline]\\n805:     #[must_use]\\n806:     #[unstable(feature = \\\"local_waker\\\", issue = \\\"118959\\\")]\\n807:     pub fn will_wake(&self, other: &LocalWaker) -> bool {\\n808:         // We optimize this by comparing vtable addresses instead of vtable contents.\\n809:         // This is permitted since the function is documented as best-effort.\\n810:         let RawWaker { data: a_data, vtable: a_vtable } = self.waker;\\n811:         let RawWaker { data: b_data, vtable: b_vtable } = other.waker;\\n812:         a_data == b_data && ptr::eq(a_vtable, b_vtable)\\n813:     }\\n814: \\n815:     /// Creates a new `LocalWaker` from the provided `data` pointer and `vtable`.\\n816:     ///\\n817:     /// The `data` pointer can be used to store arbitrary data as required\\n818:     /// by the executor. This could be e.g. a type-erased pointer to an `Arc`\\n819:     /// that is associated with the task.\\n820:     /// The value of this pointer will get passed to all functions that are part\\n821:     /// of the `vtable` as the first parameter.\\n822:     ///\\n823:     /// The `vtable` customizes the behavior of a `LocalWaker`. For each\\n824:     /// operation on the `LocalWaker`, the associated function in the `vtable`\\n825:     /// will be called.\\n826:     ///\\n827:     /// # Safety\\n828:     ///\\n829:     /// The behavior of the returned `Waker` is undefined if the contract defined\\n830:     /// in [`RawWakerVTable`]'s documentation is not upheld.\\n831:     ///\\n832:     #[inline]\\n833:     #[must_use]\\n834:     #[unstable(feature = \\\"local_waker\\\", issue = \\\"118959\\\")]\\n835:     pub const unsafe fn new(data: *const (), vtable: &'static RawWakerVTable) -> Self {\\n836:         LocalWaker { waker: RawWaker { data, vtable } }\\n837:     }\\n838: \\n839:     /// Creates a new `LocalWaker` from [`RawWaker`].\\n840:     ///\\n841:     /// The behavior of the returned `LocalWaker` is undefined if the contract defined\\n842:     /// in [`RawWaker`]'s and [`RawWakerVTable`]'s documentation is not upheld.\\n843:     /// Therefore this method is unsafe.\\n844:     #[inline]\\n845:     #[must_use]\\n846:     #[unstable(feature = \\\"local_waker\\\", issue = \\\"118959\\\")]\\n847:     pub const unsafe fn from_raw(waker: RawWaker) -> LocalWaker {\\n848:         Self { waker }\\n849:     }\\n850: \\n851:     /// Returns a reference to a `LocalWaker` that does nothing when used.\\n852:     ///\\n853:     // Note!  Much of the documentation for this method is duplicated\\n854:     // in the docs for `Waker::noop`.\\n855:     // If you edit it, consider editing the other copy too.\\n856:     //\\n857:     /// This is mostly useful for writing tests that need a [`Context`] to poll\\n858:     /// some futures, but are not expecting those futures to wake the waker or\\n859:     /// do not need to do anything again,\\n863:     /// So it should only be used when such a notification will not be needed to make progress.\\n864:     ///\\n865:     /// If an owned `LocalWaker` is needed, `clone()` this std::task::{ContextBuilder, LocalWaker, Waker, Poll};\\n873:     ///\\n874:     /// let mut cx = ContextBuilder::from_waker(Waker::noop())\\n875:     ///     .local_waker(LocalWaker::noop())\\n876: crate::panic::AssertUnwindSafe;\\n7: use crate::{fmt, ptr};\\n8: \\n9: /// A `RawWaker` allows the implementor of a task executor to create a [`Waker`]\\n10: /// or a [`LocalWaker`] which provides customized wakeup behavior.\\n11: ///\\n12: /// It consists of a data pointer and a [virtual function pointer table (vtable)][vtable]\\n13: /// that customizes the behavior of the `RawWaker`.\\n14: ///\\n15: /// `RawWaker`s are unsafe to use.\\n16: /// Implementing the [`Wake`] trait is a safe alternative that requires memory allocation.\\n17: ///\\n18: /// [vtable]: \\\"1.36.0\\\")]\\n22: pub struct RawWaker {\\n23:     /// A data pointer, which can be used to store arbitrary data as required\\n24:     /// by the executor. This could be e.g. a type-erased pointer to an `Arc`\\n25:     /// that is associated with the task.\\n26:     /// The value of this field gets passed to all functions that are part of\\n27:     /// the vtable as the first parameter.\\n28:     data: *const (),\\n29:     /// Virtual function pointer table that customizes the behavior of this waker.\\n30:     vtable: &'static RawWakerVTable,\\n31: }\\n32: \\n33: impl RawWaker {\\n34:     /// Creates a new `RawWaker` from the provided `data` pointer and `vtable`.\\n35:     ///\\n36:     /// The `data` pointer can be used to store arbitrary data as required\\n37:     /// by the executor. This could be e.g. a type-erased pointer to an `Arc`\\n38:     /// that is associated with the task.\\n39:     /// The value of this pointer will get passed to all functions that are part\\n40:     /// of the `vtable` as the first parameter.\\n41:     ///\\n42:     /// It is important to consider that the `data` pointer must point to a\\n43:     /// thread safe type such as an `Arc<T: Send + Sync>`\\n44:     /// when used to construct a [`Waker`]. This restriction is lifted when\\n45:     /// constructing a [`LocalWaker`], which allows using types that do not implement\\n46:     /// <code>[Send] + [Sync]</code> like `Rc<T>`.\\n47:     ///\\n48:     /// The `vtable` customizes the behavior of a `Waker` which gets created\\n49:     /// from a `RawWaker`. For each operation on the `Waker`, the associated\\n50:     /// function in the `vtable` of the underlying `RawWaker` will be called.\\n51:     #[inline]\\n52:     #[rustc_promotable]\\n53:     #[stable(feature = \\\"futures_api\\\", since = \\\"1.36.0\\\")]\\n54:     #[rustc_const_stable(feature = \\\"futures_api\\\", since = \\\"1.36.0\\\")]\\n55:     #[must_use]\\n56:     pub const fn new(data: *const (), vtable: &'static RawWakerVTable) -> RawWaker {\\n57:         RawWaker { data, vtable }\\n58:     }\\n59: \\n60:     #[stable(feature = \\\"noop_waker\\\", since = \\\"1.85.0\\\")]\\n61:     const NOOP: RawWaker = {\\n62:         const VTABLE: RawWakerVTable = RawWakerVTable::new(\\n63:             // Cloning just returns a new no-op raw waker\\n64:             |_| RawWaker::NOOP,\\n65:             // `wake` does nothing\\n66:             |_| {},\\n67:             // `wake_by_ref` does nothing\\n68:             |_| {},\\n69:             // Dropping does nothing as we don't allocate anything\\n70:             |_| {},\\n71:         );\\n72:         RawWaker::new(ptr::null(), &VTABLE)\\n73:     };\\n74: }\\n75: \\n76: /// A virtual function pointer table (vtable) that specifies the behavior\\n77: /// of a [`RawWaker`].\\n78: ///\\n79: /// The pointer passed to all functions inside the vtable is the `data` pointer\\n80: /// from the enclosing [`RawWaker`] object.\\n81: ///\\n82: /// The functions inside this struct are only intended to be called on the `data`\\n83: /// pointer of a properly constructed [`RawWaker`] object from inside the\\n84: /// [`RawWaker`] implementation. Calling one of the contained functions using\\n85: /// any other `data` pointer will cause undefined behavior.\\n86: ///\\n87: /// Note that while this type implements `PartialEq`, comparing function pointers, and hence\\n88: /// comparing structs like this that contain function pointers, is unreliable: pointers to the same\\n89: /// function can compare inequal (because functions are duplicated in multiple codegen units), and\\n90: /// pointers to *different* functions can compare equal (since identical functions can be\\n91: /// deduplicated within a codegen unit).\\n92: ///\\n93: /// # Thread safety\\n94: /// If the [`RawWaker`] will be used to construct a [`Waker`] then\\n95: /// these functions must all be thread-safe (even though [`RawWaker`] is\\n96: /// <code>\\\\![Send] + \\\\![Sync]</code>). This is because [`Waker`] is <code>[Send] + [Sync]</code>,\\n97: /// and it may be moved to arbitrary threads or invoked by `&` reference. For example,\\n98: /// this means that if the `clone` and `drop` functions manage a reference count,\\n99: /// they must do so atomically.\\n100: ///\\n101: /// However, if the [`RawWaker`] will be used to construct a [`LocalWaker`] instead, then\\n102: /// these functions don't need to be thread safe. This means that <code>\\\\![Send] + \\\\![Sync]</code>\\n103: ///  data can be stored in the data pointer, and reference counting does not need any atomic\\n104: /// synchronization. This is because [`LocalWaker`] is not thread safe itself, so it cannot\\n105: /// be sent across threads.\\n106: #[stable(feature = \\\"futures_api\\\", since = \\\"1.36.0\\\")]\\n107: #[allow(unpredictable_function_pointer_comparisons)]\\n108: #[derive(PartialEq, Copy, Clone, Debug)]\\n109: pub struct RawWakerVTable {\\n110:     /// This function will be called when the [`RawWaker`] gets cloned, e.g. when\\n111:     /// the [`Waker`] in which the [`RawWaker`] is stored gets cloned.\\n112:     ///\\n113:     /// The implementation of this function must retain all resources that are\\n114:     /// required for this additional instance of a [`RawWaker`] and associated\\n115:     /// task. Calling `wake` on the resulting [`RawWaker`] should result in a wakeup\\n116:     /// of the same task that would have been awoken by the original [`RawWaker`].\\n117:     clone: unsafe fn(*const ()) -> RawWaker,\\n118: \\n119:     /// This function will be called when `wake` is called on the [`Waker`].\\n120:     /// It must wake up the task associated with this [`RawWaker`].\\n121:     ///\\n122:     /// The implementation of this function must make sure to release any\\n123:     /// resources that are associated with this instance of a [`RawWaker`] and\\n124:     /// associated task.\\n125:     wake: unsafe fn(*const ()),\\n126: \\n127:     /// This function will be called when `wake_by_ref` is called on the [`Waker`].\\n128:     /// It must wake up the task associated with this [`RawWaker`].\\n129:     ///\\n130:     /// This function is similar to `wake`, but must not consume the provided data\\n131:     /// pointer.\\n132:     wake_by_ref: unsafe fn(*const ()),\\n133: \\n134:     /// This function will be called when a [`Waker`] gets dropped.\\n135:     ///\\n136:     /// The implementation of this function must make sure to release any\\n137:     /// resources that are associated with this instance of a [`RawWaker`] and\\n138:     /// associated task.\\n139:     drop: unsafe fn(*const ()),\\n140: }\\n141: \\n142: impl RawWakerVTable {\\n143:     /// Creates a new `RawWakerVTable` from the provided `clone`, `wake`,\\n144:     /// `wake_by_ref`, and `drop` functions.\\n145:     ///\\n146:     /// If the [`RawWaker`] will be used to construct a [`Waker`] then\\n147:     /// these functions must all be thread-safe (even though [`RawWaker`] is\\n148:     /// <code>\\\\![Send] + \\\\![Sync]</code>). For example,\\n150:     /// this means that if the `clone` and `drop` functions manage a reference count,\\n151:     /// they must do so atomically.\\n152:     ///\\n153:     /// However, if the [`RawWaker`] will be used to construct a [`LocalWaker`] instead, then\\n154:     /// these functions don't need to be thread safe. `wake`\\n169:     ///\\n170:     /// This function will be called when `wake` is called on the [`Waker`].\\n171:     /// It must wake up the task associated with this [`RawWaker`].\\n172:     ///\\n173:     /// The implementation of this function must make sure to release any\\n174:     /// resources that are associated with this instance of a [`RawWaker`] and\\n175:     /// associated #[stable(feature = \\\"futures_api\\\", since = \\\"1.36.0\\\")]\\n195:     #[rustc_const_stable(feature = \\\"futures_api\\\", since = \\\"1.36.0\\\")]\\n196:     pub const fn new(\\n197:    }\\n368: \\n369:     /// Builds the `Context`.\\n370:     #[inline]\\n371:     #[unstable(feature = \\\"local_waker\\\", issue = \\\"118959\\\")]\\n372:     pub const fn build(self) -> Context<'a> {\\n373:         let ContextBuilder { waker, local_waker, ext, _marker, _marker2 } = self;\\n374:         Context { waker, local_waker, ext: AssertUnwindSafe(ext), _marker, _marker2 }\\n375:     }\\n376: }\\n377: \\n378: /// A `Waker` is a handle for waking up a task by notifying its executor that it\\n379: /// is ready to be run.\\n380: ///\\n381: /// This handle encapsulates a [`RawWaker`] instance, which defines the\\n382: /// executor-specific wakeup behavior.\\n383: ///\\n384: /// The typical life of a `Waker` is that it is constructed by an executor, wrapped in a\\n385: /// [`Context`], then passed to [`Future::poll()`]. Then, if the future chooses to return\\n386: /// [`Poll::Pending`], it must also store the waker somehow and call [`Waker::wake()`] when\\n387: /// the future should be polled again.\\n388: ///\\n389: /// Implements [`Clone`], [`Send`], and [`Sync`]; therefore, a waker may be invoked\\n390: /// from any thread, including ones not in any way managed by the executor. For example,\\n391: /// this might be done to wake a future when a blocking function call completes on another\\n392: /// thread.\\n393: ///\\n394: /// Note that it is preferable to use `waker.clone_from(&new_waker)` instead\\n395: /// of `*waker = new_waker.clone()`, as the former will avoid cloning the waker\\n396: /// unnecessarily if the two wakers [wake the same task](Self::will_wake).\\n397: ///\\n398: /// Constructing a `Waker` from a [`RawWaker`] is unsafe.\\n399: /// Implementing the [`Wake`] trait is a safe alternative that requires memory allocation.\\n400: ///\\n401: /// [`Future::poll()`]: core::future::Future::poll\\n402: /// [`Poll::Pending`]: core::task::Poll::Pending\\n403: /// [`Wake`]: ../../alloc/task/trait.Wake.html\\n404: #[repr(transparent)]\\n405: #[stable(feature = \\\"futures_api\\\", since = \\\"1.36.0\\\")]\\n406: #[rustc_diagnostic_item = \\\"Waker\\\"]\\n407: pub struct Waker {\\n408:     waker: RawWaker,\\n409: }\\n410: \\n411: #[stable(feature = \\\"futures_api\\\", since = \\\"1.36.0\\\")]\\n412: impl Unpin for Waker {}\\n413: #[stable(feature = \\\"futures_api\\\", since = \\\"1.36.0\\\")]\\n414: unsafe impl Send for Waker {}\\n415: #[stable(feature = \\\"futures_api\\\", since = \\\"1.36.0\\\")]\\n416: unsafe impl Sync for Waker {}\\n417: \\n418: impl Waker {\\n419:     /// Wakes up the task associated with this `Waker`.\\n420:     ///\\n421:     /// As long as the executor keeps running and the task is not finished, it is\\n422:     /// guaranteed that each invocation of [`wake()`](Self::wake) (or\\n423:     /// [`wake_by_ref()`](Self::wake_by_ref)) will be followed by at least one\\n424:     /// [`poll()`] of the task to which this `Waker` belongs. This makes\\n425:     /// it possible to temporarily yield to other tasks while running potentially\\n426:     /// unbounded processing loops.\\n427:     ///\\n428:     /// Note that the above implies that multiple wake-ups may be coalesced into a\\n429:     /// single [`poll()`] invocation by the runtime.\\n430:     ///\\n431:     /// Also note that yielding to competing tasks is not guaranteed: it is the\\n432:     /// executor’s choice which task to run and the executor may choose to run the\\n433:     /// current task again.\\n434:     ///\\n435:     /// [`poll()`]: crate::future::Future::poll\\n436:     #[inline]\\n437:     #[stable(feature = \\\"futures_api\\\", since = \\\"1.36.0\\\")]\\n438:     pub fn wake(self) {\\n439:         // The actual wakeup call is delegated through a virtual function call\\n440:         // to the implementation which is defined by the executor.\\n441: \\n442:         // Don't call `drop` -- the waker will be consumed by `wake`.\\n443:         let this = ManuallyDrop::new(self);\\n444: \\n445:         // SAFETY: This is safe because `Waker::from_raw` is the only way\\n446:         // to initialize `wake` and `data` requiring the user to acknowledge\\n447:         // that the contract of `RawWaker` is upheld.\\n448:         unsafe { (this.waker.vtable.wake)(this.waker.data) };\\n449:     }\\n450: \\n451:     /// Wakes up the task associated with this `Waker` without consuming the `Waker`.\\n452:     ///\\n453:     /// This is similar to [`wake()`](Self::wake), but may be slightly less efficient in\\n454:     /// the case where an owned `Waker` is available. This method should be preferred to\\n455:     /// calling `waker.clone().wake()`.\\n456:     #[inline]\\n457:     #[stable(feature = \\\"futures_api\\\", since = \\\"1.36.0\\\")]\\n458:     pub fn wake_by_ref(&self) {\\n459:         // The actual wakeup call is delegated through a virtual function call\\n460:         // to the implementation which is defined by the executor.\\n461: \\n462:         // SAFETY: see `wake`\\n463:         unsafe { (self.waker.vtable.wake_by_ref)(self.waker.data) }\\n464:     }\\n465: \\n466:     /// Returns `true` if this `Waker` and another `Waker` would awake the same task.\\n467:     ///\\n468:     /// This function works on a best-effort basis, and may return false even\\n469:     /// when the `Waker`s would awaken the same task. However, if this function\\n470:     /// returns `true`, it is guaranteed that the `Waker`s will awaken the same task.\\n471:     ///\\n472:     /// This function is primarily used for optimization purposes — for example,\\n473:     /// this type's [`clone_from`](Self::clone_from) implementation uses it to\\n474:     /// avoid cloning the waker when they would wake the same task anyway.\\n475:     #[inline]\\n476:     #[must_use]\\n477:     #[stable(feature = \\\"futures_api\\\", since = \\\"1.36.0\\\")]\\n478:     pub fn will_wake(&self, other: &Waker) -> bool {\\n479:         // We optimize this by comparing vtable addresses instead of vtable contents.\\n480:         // This is permitted since the function is documented as best-effort.\\n481:         let RawWaker { data: a_data, vtable: a_vtable } = self.waker;\\n482:         let RawWaker { data: b_data, vtable: b_vtable } = other.waker;\\n483:         a_data == b_data && ptr::eq(a_vtable, b_vtable)\\n484:     }\\n485: \\n486:     /// Creates a new `Waker` from the provided `data` pointer and `vtable`.\\n487:     ///\\n488:     /// The `data` pointer can be used to store arbitrary data as required\\n489:     /// by the executor. This could be e.g. a type-erased pointer to an `Arc`\\n490:     /// that is associated with the task.\\n491:     /// The value of this pointer will get passed to all functions that are part\\n492:     /// of the `vtable` as the first parameter.\\n493:     ///\\n494:     /// It is important to consider that the `data` pointer must point to a\\n495:     /// thread safe type such as an `Arc`.\\n496:     ///\\n497:     /// The `vtable` customizes the behavior of a `Waker`. For each operation\\n498:     /// on the `Waker`, the associated function in the `vtable` will be called.\\n499:     ///\\n500:     /// # Safety\\n501:     ///\\n502:     /// The behavior of the returned `Waker` is undefined if the contract defined\\n503:     /// in [`RawWakerVTable`]'s documentation is not upheld.\\n504:     ///\\n505:     /// (Authors wishing to avoid unsafe code may implement the [`Wake`] trait instead, at the\\n506:     /// cost of a required heap allocation.)\\n507:     ///\\n508:     /// [`Wake`]: ../../alloc/task/trait.Wake.html\\n509:     #[inline]\\n510:     #[must_use]\\n511:     #[stable(feature = \\\"waker_getters\\\", since = \\\"1.83.0\\\")]\\n512:     #[rustc_const_stable(feature = \\\"waker_getters\\\", since = \\\"1.83.0\\\")]\\n513:     pub const unsafe fn new(data: *const (), vtable: &'static RawWakerVTable) -> Self {\\n514:         Waker { waker: RawWaker { data, vtable } }\\n515:     }\\n516: \\n517:     /// Creates a new `Waker` from [`RawWaker`].\\n518:     ///\\n519:     /// # Safety\\n520:     ///\\n521:     /// The behavior of the returned `Waker` is undefined if the contract defined\\n522:     /// in [`RawWaker`]'s and [`RawWakerVTable`]'s documentation is not upheld.\\n523:     ///\\n524:     /// (Authors wishing to avoid unsafe code may implement the [`Wake`] trait instead, at the\\n525:     /// cost of a required heap allocation.)\\n526:     ///\\n527:     /// [`Wake`]: ../../alloc/task/trait.Wake.html\\n528:     #[inline]\\n529:     #[must_use]\\n530:     #[stable(feature = \\\"futures_api\\\", since = \\\"1.36.0\\\")]\\n531:     #[rustc_const_stable(feature = \\\"const_waker\\\", since = \\\"1.82.0\\\")]\\n532:     pub const unsafe fn from_raw(waker: RawWaker) -> Waker {\\n533:         Waker { waker }\\n534:     }\\n535: \\n536:     /// Returns a reference to a `Waker` that does nothing when used.\\n537:     ///\\n538:     // Note!  Much of the documentation for this method is duplicated\\n539:     // in the docs for `LocalWaker::noop`.\\n540:     // If you edit it, consider editing the other copy too.\\n541:     //\\n542:     /// This is mostly useful for writing tests that need a [`Context`] to poll\\n543:     /// some futures, but are not expecting those futures to wake the waker or\\n544:     /// do not need to do anything specific if it happens.\\n545:     ///\\n546:     /// More generally, using `Waker::noop()` to poll a future\\n547:     /// means discarding the notification of when the future should be polled again.\\n548:     /// So it should only be used when such a notification will not be needed to make progress.\\n549:     ///\\n550:     /// If an owned `Waker` is needed, `clone()` this one.\\n551:     ///\\n552:     /// # Examples\\n553:     ///\\n554:     /// ```\\n555:     /// use std::future::Future;\\n556:     /// use std::task;\\n557:     ///\\n558:     /// let mut cx = task::Context::from_waker(task::Waker::noop());\\n559:     ///\\n560:     /// let mut future = Box::pin(async { 10 });\\n561:     /// assert_eq!(future.as_mut().poll(&mut cx), task::Poll::Ready(10));\\n562:     /// ```\\n563:     #[inline]\\n564:     #[must_use]\\n565:     #[stable(feature = \\\"noop_waker\\\", since = \\\"1.85.0\\\")]\\n566:     #[rustc_const_stable(feature = \\\"noop_waker\\\", since = \\\"1.85.0\\\")]\\n567:     pub const fn noop() -> &'static Waker {\\n568:         const WAKER: &Waker = &Waker { waker: RawWaker::NOOP };\\n569:         WAKER\\n570:     }\\n571: \\n572:     /// Gets the `data` pointer used to create this `Waker`.\\n573:     #[inline]\\n574:     #[must_use]\\n575:     #[stable(feature = \\\"waker_getters\\\", since = \\\"1.83.0\\\")]\\n576:     pub fn data(&self) -> *const () {\\n577:         self.waker.data\\n578:     }\\n579: \\n580:     /// Gets the `vtable` pointer used to create this `Waker`.\\n581:     #[inline]\\n582:     #[must_use]\\n583:     #[stable(feature = \\\"waker_getters\\\", since = \\\"1.83.0\\\")]\\n584:     pub fn vtable(&self) -> &'static RawWakerVTable {\\n585:         self.waker.vtable\\n586:     }\\n587: \\n588:     /// Constructs a `Waker` from a function pointer.\\n589:     #[inline]\\n590:     #[must_use]\\n591:     #[unstable(feature = \\\"waker_from_fn_ptr\\\", issue = \\\"148457\\\")]\\n592:     pub const fn from_fn_ptr(f: fn()) -> Self {\\n593:         // SAFETY: Unsafe is used for transmutes, pointer came from `fn()` so it\\n594:         //         is sound to transmute it back to `fn()`.\\n595:         static VTABLE: RawWakerVTable = unsafe {\\n596:             RawWakerVTable::new(\\n597:                 |this| {},\\n601:             )\\n602:         };\\n603:         let raw = RawWaker::new(f as *const (), &VTABLE);\\n604: \\n605:         // SAFETY: `clone` is just a copy, `drop` is a no-op while `wake` and\\n606:         //         `wake_by_ref` just call the function pointer.\\n607:         unsafe { Self::from_raw(raw) }\\n608:     }\\n609: }\\n610: \\n611: #[stable(feature = \\\"futures_api\\\", since = \\\"1.36.0\\\")]\\n612: impl Clone for Waker {\\n613:     #[inline]\\n614:     fn clone(&self) -> Self {\\n615:         Waker {\\n616:             // SAFETY: This is safe because `Waker::from_raw` is the only way\\n617:             // to initialize `clone` and `data` requiring the user to acknowledge\\n618:             // that the contract of [`RawWaker`] is upheld.\\n619:             waker: unsafe { (self.waker.vtable.clone)(self.waker.data) },\\n620:         }\\n621:     }\\n622: \\n623:     /// Assigns a clone of `source` to `self`, unless [`self.will_wake(source)`][Waker::will_wake] anyway.\\n624:     ///\\n625:     /// This method is preferred over simply assigning `source.clone()` to `self`,\\n626:     /// as it avoids cloning the waker if `self` is already the same waker.\\n627:     ///\\n628:     /// # Examples\\n629:     ///\\n630:     /// ```\\n631:     /// use std::future::Future;\\n632:     /// use std::pin::Pin;\\n633:     /// use std::sync::{Arc, Mutex};\\n634:     /// use std::task::{Context, Poll, Waker};\\n635:     ///\\n636:     /// struct Waiter {\\n637:     ///     shared: Arc<Mutex<Shared>>,\\n638:     /// }\\n639:     ///\\n640:     /// struct Shared {\\n641:     ///     waker: Waker,\\n642:     ///     // ...\\n643:     /// }\\n644:     ///\\n645:     /// impl Future for Waiter {\\n646:     ///     type Output = ();\\n647:     ///     fn poll(self: Pin<&mut Self>, cx: &mut Context<'_>) -> Poll<()> {\\n648:     ///         let mut shared = self.shared.lock().unwrap();\\n649:     ///\\n650:   ///     }\\n656:     /// }\\n657:     ///\\n658:     /// ```\\n659:     #[inline]\\n660:     fn clone_from(&mut self, source: &Self) {\\n661:         if !self.will_wake(source) {\\n662:             *self = source.clone();\\n663:         }\\n664:     }\\n665: }\\n666: \\n667: #[stable(feature = \\\"futures_api\\\", since = \\\"1.36.0\\\")]\\n668: impl Drop for Waker {\\n669:     #[inline]\\n670:     fn drop(&mut self) {\\n671:         // SAFETY: This is safe because `Waker::from_raw` is the only way\\n672:         // to initialize `drop` and `data` requiring the user to acknowledge\\n673:         // that the contract of `RawWaker` is upheld.\\n674:         unsafe { (self.waker.vtable.drop)(self.waker.data) }\\n675:     }\\n676: }\\n677: \\n678: #[stable(feature = \\\"futures_api\\\", since = \\\"1.36.0\\\")]\\n679: impl fmt::Debug for Waker {\\n680:     fn fmt(&self, f: &mut fmt::Formatter<'_>) -> fmt::Result {\\n681:         let vtable_ptr = self.waker.vtable as *const RawWakerVTable;\\n682:         f.debug_struct(\\\"Waker\\\")\\n683:             .field(\\\"data\\\", &self.waker.data)\\n684:             .field(\\\"vtable\\\", &vtable_ptr)\\n685:             .finish()\\n686:     }\\n687: }\\n688: \\n689: /// A `LocalWaker` is analogous to a [`Waker`], but it does not implement [`Send`] or [`Sync`].\\n690: ///\\n691: /// This handle encapsulates a [`RawWaker`] instance, which defines the\\n692: /// executor-specific wakeup behavior.\\n693: ///\\n694: /// Local wakers can be requested from a `Context` with the [`local_waker`] method.\\n695: ///\\n696: /// The typical life of a `LocalWaker` is that it is constructed by an executor, wrapped in a\\n697: /// [`Context`] using [`ContextBuilder`], then passed to [`Future::poll()`]. Then, if the future chooses to return\\n698: /// [`Poll::Pending`], it must also store the waker somehow and call [`LocalWaker::wake()`] when\\n699: /// the future should be polled again.\\n700: ///\\n701: /// Implements [`Clone`], but neither [`Send`] nor [`Sync`]; therefore, a local waker may\\n702: /// not be moved to other threads. In general, when deciding to use wakers or local wakers,\\n703: /// local wakers are preferable unless the waker needs to be sent across threads. This is because\\n704: /// wakers can incur in additional cost related to memory synchronization.\\n705: ///\\n706: /// Note that it is preferable to use `local_waker.clone_from(&new_waker)` instead\\n707: /// of `*local_waker = new_waker.clone()`, as the former will avoid cloning the waker\\n708: /// unnecessarily if the two wakers [wake the same task](Self::will_wake).\\n709: ///\\n710: /// # Examples\\n711: /// Usage of a local waker to implement a future analogous to `std::thread::yield_now()`.\\n712: /// ```\\n713: /// #![feature(local_waker)]\\n714: /// use std::future::{Future, poll_fn};\\n715: /// use std::task::Poll;\\n716: ///\\n717: /// // a future that returns pending once.\\n718: /// fn yield_now() -> impl Future<Output=()> + Unpin {\\n719: ///     let mut yielded = false;\\n720: ///     poll_fn(move |cx| {\\n721: ///         if !yielded {\\n722: ///             yielded = true;\\n723: ///             cx.local_waker().wake_by_ref();\\n724: ///             return Poll::Pending;\\n725: ///         }\\n726: ///         return Poll::Ready(())\\n727: ///     })\\n728: /// }\\n729: ///\\n730: /// # async fn __() {\\n731: /// yield_now().await;\\n732: /// # }\\n733: /// ```\\n734: ///\\n735: /// [`Future::poll()`]: core::future::Future::poll\\n736: /// [`Poll::Pending`]: core::task::Poll::Pending\\n737: /// [`local_waker`]: core::task::Context::local_waker\\n738: #[unstable(feature = \\\"local_waker\\\", issue = \\\"118959\\\")]\\n739: #[repr(transparent)]\\n740: pub struct LocalWaker {\\n741:     waker: RawWaker,\\n742: }\\n743: \\n744: #[unstable(feature = \\\"local_waker\\\", issue = \\\"118959\\\")]\\n745: impl Unpin for LocalWaker {}\\n746: \\n747: impl LocalWaker {\\n748:     /// Wakes up the task associated with this `LocalWaker`.\\n749:     ///\\n750:     /// As long as the executor keeps running and the task is not finished, it is\\n751:     /// guaranteed that each invocation of [`wake()`](Self::wake) (or\\n752:     /// [`wake_by_ref()`](Self::wake_by_ref)) will be followed by at least one\\n753:     /// [`poll()`] of the task to which this `LocalWaker` belongs. This makes\\n754:     /// it possible to temporarily yield to other tasks while running potentially\\n755:     /// unbounded processing loops.\\n756:     ///\\n757:     /// Note that the above implies that multiple wake-ups may be coalesced into a\\n758:     /// single [`poll()`] invocation by the runtime.\\n759:     ///\\n760:     /// Also note that yielding to competing tasks is not guaranteed: it is the\\n761:     /// executor’s choice which task to run and the executor may choose to run the\\n762:     /// current task again.\\n763:     ///\\n764:     /// [`poll()`]: crate::future::Future::poll\\n765:     #[inline]\\n766:     #[unstable(feature = \\\"local_waker\\\", issue = \\\"118959\\\")]\\n767:     pub fn wake(self) {\\n768:         // The actual wakeup call is delegated through a virtual function call\\n769:         // to the implementation which is defined by the executor.\\n770: \\n771:         // Don't call `drop` -- the waker will be consumed by `wake`.\\n772:         let this = ManuallyDrop::new(self);\\n773: \\n774:         // SAFETY: This is safe because `Waker::from_raw` is the only way\\n775:         // to initialize `wake` and `data` requiring the user to acknowledge\\n776:         // that the contract of `RawWaker` is upheld.\\n777:         unsafe { (this.waker.vtable.wake)(this.waker.data) };\\n778:     }\\n779: \\n780:     /// Wakes up the task associated with this `LocalWaker` without consuming the `LocalWaker`.\\n781:     ///\\n782:     /// This is similar to [`wake()`](Self::wake), but may be slightly less efficient in\\n783:     /// the case where an owned `Waker` is available. This method should be preferred to\\n784:     /// calling `waker.clone().wake()`.\\n785:     #[inline]\\n786:     #[unstable(feature = \\\"local_waker\\\", issue = \\\"118959\\\")]\\n787:     pub fn wake_by_ref(&self) {\\n788:         // The actual wakeup call is delegated through a virtual function call\\n789:         // to the implementation which is defined by the executor.\\n790: \\n791:         // SAFETY: see `wake`\\n792:         unsafe { (self.waker.vtable.wake_by_ref)(self.waker.data) }\\n793:     }\\n794: \\n795:     /// Returns `true` if this `LocalWaker` and another `LocalWaker` would awake the same task.\\n796:     ///\\n797:     /// This function works on a best-effort basis, and may return false even\\n798:     /// when the `Waker`s would awaken the same task. However, if this function\\n799:     /// returns `true`, it is guaranteed that the `Waker`s will awaken the same task.\\n800:     ///\\n801:     /// This function is primarily used for optimization purposes — for example,\\n802:     /// this type's [`clone_from`](Self::clone_from) implementation uses it to\\n803:     /// avoid cloning the waker when they would wake the same task anyway.\\n804:     #[inline]\\n805:     #[must_use]\\n806:     #[unstable(feature = \\\"local_waker\\\", issue = \\\"118959\\\")]\\n807:     pub fn will_wake(&self, other: &LocalWaker) -> bool {\\n808:         // We optimize this by comparing vtable addresses instead of vtable contents.\\n809:         // This is permitted since the function is documented as best-effort.\\n810:         let RawWaker { data: a_data, vtable: a_vtable } = self.waker;\\n811:         let RawWaker { data: b_data, vtable: b_vtable } = other.waker;\\n812:         a_data == b_data && ptr::eq(a_vtable, b_vtable)\\n813:     }\\n814: \\n815:     /// Creates a new `LocalWaker` from the provided `data` pointer and `vtable`.\\n816:     ///\\n817:     /// The `data` pointer can be used to store arbitrary data as required\\n818:     /// by the executor. This could be e.g. a type-erased pointer to an `Arc`\\n819:     /// that is associated with the task.\\n820:     /// The value of this pointer will get passed to all functions that are part\\n821:     /// of the `vtable` as the first parameter.\\n822:     ///\\n823:     /// The `vtable` customizes the behavior of a `LocalWaker`. For each\\n824:     /// operation on the `LocalWaker`, the associated function in the `vtable`\\n825:     /// will be called.\\n826:     ///\\n827:     /// # Safety\\n828:     ///\\n829:     /// The behavior of the returned `Waker` is undefined if the contract defined\\n830:     /// in [`RawWakerVTable`]'s documentation is not upheld.\\n831:     ///\\n832:     #[inline]\\n833:     #[must_use]\\n834:     #[unstable(feature = \\\"local_waker\\\", issue = \\\"118959\\\")]\\n835:     pub const unsafe fn new(data: *const (), vtable: &'static RawWakerVTable) -> Self {\\n836:         LocalWaker { waker: RawWaker { data, vtable } }\\n837:     }\\n838: \\n839:     /// Creates a new `LocalWaker` from [`RawWaker`].\\n840:     ///\\n841:     /// The behavior of the returned `LocalWaker` is undefined if the contract defined\\n842:     /// in [`RawWaker`]'s and [`RawWakerVTable`]'s documentation is not upheld.\\n843:     /// Therefore this method is unsafe.\\n844:     #[inline]\\n845:     #[must_use]\\n846:     #[unstable(feature = \\\"local_waker\\\", issue = \\\"118959\\\")]\\n847:     pub const unsafe fn from_raw(waker: RawWaker) -> LocalWaker {\\n848:         Self { waker }\\n849:     }\\n850: \\n851:     /// Returns a reference to a `LocalWaker` that does nothing when used.\\n852:     ///\\n853:     // Note! #[inline]\\n882:     #[must_use]\\n883:     #[unstable(feature = \\\"local_waker\\\", issue = \\\"118959\\\")]\\n884:     pub const fn noop() -> &'static LocalWaker {\\n885:         const WAKER: crate::panic::AssertUnwindSafe;\n7: use crate::{fmt, ptr};\n8: \n9: /// A `RawWaker` allows the implementor of a task executor to create a [`Waker`]\n10: /// or a [`LocalWaker`] which provides ///\n15: /// `RawWaker`s are unsafe to use.\n16: /// Implementing the [`Wake`] trait is a safe alternative that requires memory allocation.\n17: ///\n18: /// [vtable]: \"1.36.0\")]\n22: pub struct RawWaker {\n23:     /// A data pointer, which can be used to store arbitrary data as required\n24:     /// by the executor. This could be e.g. a type-erased pointer to an `Arc`\n25:     /// that is associated with the task.\n26:     /// The value of this field gets passed to all functions that are part of\n27:     /// the vtable as the first parameter.\n28:     data: *const (),\n29:     /// Virtual function pointer table that customizes the behavior of this waker.\n30:     vtable: &'static RawWakerVTable,\n31: }\n32: \n33: impl RawWaker {\n34:     /// Creates a new `RawWaker` from the provided `data` pointer and `vtable`.\n35:     ///\n36:     /// The `data` pointer can be used to store arbitrary data as required\n37:     /// by the executor. This could be e.g. a type-erased pointer to an `Arc`\n38:     /// that is associated with the task.\n39:     /// The value of this pointer will get passed to all functions that are part\n40:     /// of the `vtable` as the first parameter.\n41:     ///\n42:     /// It is important to consider that the `data` pointer must point to a\n43:     /// thread safe type such as an `Arc<T: Send + Sync>`\n44:     /// when used to construct a [`Waker`]. This restriction is lifted when\n45:     /// constructing a [`LocalWaker`], which allows using types that do not implement\n46:     /// <code>[Send] + [Sync]</code> like `Rc<T>`.\n47:     ///\n48:     /// The `vtable` customizes the behavior of a `Waker` which gets created\n49:     /// from a `RawWaker`. For each operation on the `Waker`, the associated\n50:     /// function in the `vtable` of the underlying `RawWaker` will be called.\n51:     #[inline]\n52:     #[rustc_promotable]\n53:     #[stable(feature = \"futures_api\", since = \"1.36.0\")]\n54:     #[rustc_const_stable(feature = \"futures_api\", since = \"1.36.0\")]\n55:     #[must_use]\n56:     pub const fn new(data: *const (), vtable: &'static RawWakerVTable) -> RawWaker {\n57:         RawWaker { data, vtable }\n58:     }\n59: \n60:     #[stable(feature = \"noop_waker\", since = \"1.85.0\")]\n61:     const NOOP: RawWaker = {\n62:         const VTABLE: RawWakerVTable = RawWakerVTable::new(\n63:             // Cloning just returns a new no-op raw waker\n64:             |_| RawWaker::NOOP,\n65:             // `wake` does nothing\n66:             |_| {},\n67:             // `wake_by_ref` does nothing\n68:             |_| {},\n69:             // Dropping does nothing as we don't allocate anything\n70:             |_| {},\n71:         );\n72:         RawWaker::new(ptr::null(), &VTABLE)\n73:     };\n74: }\n75: \n76: /// A virtual function pointer table (vtable) that specifies the behavior\n77: /// of a [`RawWaker`].\n78: ///\n79: /// The pointer passed to all functions inside the vtable is the `data` pointer\n80: /// from the enclosing [`RawWaker`] object.\n81: ///\n82: /// The functions inside this struct are only intended to be called on the `data`\n83: /// pointer of a properly constructed [`RawWaker`] object from inside the\n84: /// [`RawWaker`] implementation. Calling one of the contained functions using\n85: /// any other `data` pointer will cause undefined behavior.\n86: ///\n87: /// Note that while this type implements `PartialEq`, comparing function pointers, and hence\n88: /// comparing structs like this that contain function pointers, is unreliable: pointers to the same\n89: /// function can compare inequal (because functions are duplicated in multiple codegen units), and\n90: /// pointers to *different* functions can compare equal (since identical functions can be\n91: /// deduplicated within a codegen unit).\n92: ///\n93: /// # Thread safety\n94: /// If the [`RawWaker`] will be used to construct a [`Waker`] then\n95: /// these functions must all be thread-safe (even though [`RawWaker`] is\n96: /// <code>\\![Send] + \\![Sync]</code>). This is because [`Waker`] is <code>[Send] + [Sync]</code>,\n97: /// and it may be moved to arbitrary threads or invoked by `&` reference. For example,\n98: /// this means that if the `clone` and `drop` functions manage a reference count,\n99: /// they must do so atomically.\n100: ///\n101: /// However, if the [`RawWaker`] will be used to construct a [`LocalWaker`] instead, then\n102: /// these functions don't need to be thread safe. This means that <code>\\![Send] + \\![Sync]</code>\n103: ///  data can be stored in the data pointer, and reference counting does not need any atomic\n104: /// synchronization. This is because [`LocalWaker`] is not thread safe itself, so it cannot\n105: /// be sent across threads.\n106: #[stable(feature = \"futures_api\", since = \"1.36.0\")]\n107: #[allow(unpredictable_function_pointer_comparisons)]\n108: #[derive(PartialEq, Copy, Clone, Debug)]\n109: pub struct RawWakerVTable {\n110:     /// This function will be called when the [`RawWaker`] gets cloned, e.g. when\n111:     /// the [`Waker`] in which the [`RawWaker`] is stored gets cloned.\n112:     ///\n113:     /// The implementation of this function must retain all resources that are\n114:     /// required for this additional instance of a [`RawWaker`] and associated\n115:     /// task. ///\n177:     /// # `wake_by_ref`\n178:     ///\n179:     /// This function will be called when `wake_by_ref` is called on the [`Waker`].\n180:     /// It must wake up the task associated with this }\n204: }\n205: \n206: #[derive(Debug)]\n207: enum ExtData<'a> {\n208:     Some(&'a mut dyn Any),\n209:     None(()),\n210: }\n211: \n212: /// The context of an asynchronous task.\n213: ///\n214: /// pub struct ContextBuilder<'a> {\n302:     waker: &'a Waker,\n303:     local_waker: &'a LocalWaker,\n304:     ext: ExtData<'a>,\n305:     // Ensure we future-proof against variance changes by ()>,\n313: }\n314: \n315: impl<'a> ContextBuilder<'a> {\n316:     /// Creates a ContextBuilder from a Waker.\n317:     #[inline]\n318:     #[unstable(feature = \"local_waker\", issue = transmute(waker) };\n322:         Self {\n323:             waker,\n324:             local_waker,\n325:             ext: ExtData::None(()),\n326:             _marker: PhantomData,\n327:             _marker2: PhantomData,\n328:         }\n329:     }\n330: \n331:     /// Creates a ContextBuilder from an existing Context.\n332:     #[inline]\n333:     #[unstable(feature = \"context_ext\", issue = ExtData::None(()) => ExtData::None(()),\n338:         };\n339:         Self {\n340:             waker: cx.waker,\n341:             local_waker: cx.local_waker,\n342:             ext,\n343: -> Self {\n359:         Self { local_waker, ..self }\n360:     }\n361: \n362:     /// Sets the value for the extension data on `Context`.\n363:     #[inline]\n364:     #[unstable(feature = \"context_ext\", issue = \"123392\")]\n365:     pub const fn ext(self, data: &'a mut dyn Any) -> Self {\n366:         Self { ext: ExtData::Some(data), ..self }\n367:     }\n368: \n369:     /// Builds the `Context`.\n370:     #[inline]\n371:     #[unstable(feature = \"local_waker\", issue = \"118959\")]\n372:     pub const fn build(self) -> Context<'a> {\n373:         let ContextBuilder { waker, local_waker, ext, _marker, _marker2 } = self;\n374:         Context { waker, local_waker, ext: AssertUnwindSafe(ext), _marker, _marker2 }\n375:     }\n376: }\n377: \n378: /// A `Waker` is a handle for waking up a task by notifying its executor that it\n379: /// is ready to be run.\n380: ///\n381: /// This handle encapsulates a [`RawWaker`] instance, which defines the\n382: /// executor-specific wakeup behavior.\n383: ///\n384: /// The typical life of a `Waker` is that it is constructed by an executor, wrapped in a\n385: /// [`Context`], then passed to [`Future::poll()`]. Then, if the future chooses to return\n386: /// [`Poll::Pending`], it must also store the waker somehow and call [`Waker::wake()`] when\n387: /// the future should be polled again.\n388: ///\n389: /// Implements [`Clone`], [`Send`], and [`Sync`]; therefore, a waker may be invoked\n390: /// from any thread, including ones not in any way managed by the executor. For example,\n391: /// this might be done to wake a future when a blocking function call completes on another\n392: /// thread.\n393: ///\n394: /// Note that it is preferable to use `waker.clone_from(&new_waker)` instead\n395: /// of `*waker = new_waker.clone()`, as the former will avoid cloning the waker\n396: /// unnecessarily if the two wakers [wake the same task](Self::will_wake).\n397: ///\n398: /// Constructing a `Waker` from a [`RawWaker`] is unsafe.\n399: /// Implementing the [`Wake`] trait is a safe alternative that requires memory allocation.\n400: ///\n401: /// [`Future::poll()`]: core::future::Future::poll\n402: /// [`Poll::Pending`]: core::task::Poll::Pending\n403: /// [`Wake`]: ../../alloc/task/trait.Wake.html\n404: #[repr(transparent)]\n405: #[stable(feature = \"futures_api\", since = \"1.36.0\")]\n406: #[rustc_diagnostic_item = \"Waker\"]\n407: pub struct Waker {\n408:     waker: RawWaker,\n409: }\n410: \n411: #[stable(feature = \"futures_api\", since = \"1.36.0\")]\n412: impl Unpin for Waker {}\n413: #[stable(feature = \"futures_api\", since = \"1.36.0\")]\n414: unsafe impl Send for Waker {}\n415: #[stable(feature = \"futures_api\", since = \"1.36.0\")]\n416: unsafe impl Sync for Waker {}\n417: \n418: impl Waker {\n419:     /// Wakes up the task associated with this `Waker`.\n420:     ///\n421:     /// As long as the executor keeps running and the task is not finished, it is\n422:     /// guaranteed that each invocation of [`wake()`](Self::wake) (or\n423:     /// [`wake_by_ref()`](Self::wake_by_ref)) will be followed by at least one\n424:     /// [`poll()`] of the task to which this `Waker` belongs. This makes\n425:     /// it possible to temporarily yield to other tasks while running potentially\n426:     /// unbounded processing loops.\n427:     ///\n428:     /// Note that the above implies that multiple wake-ups may be coalesced into a\n429:     /// single [`poll()`] invocation by the runtime.\n430:     ///\n431:     /// Also note that yielding to competing tasks is not guaranteed: it is the\n432:     /// executor’s choice which task to run and the executor may choose to run the\n433:     /// current task again.\n434:     ///\n435:     /// [`poll()`]: crate::future::Future::poll\n436:     #[inline]\n437:     #[stable(feature = \"futures_api\", since = \"1.36.0\")]\n438:     pub fn wake(self) {\n439:         // The actual wakeup call is delegated through a virtual function call\n440:         // to the implementation which is defined by the executor.\n441: \n442:         // Don't call `drop` -- the waker will be consumed by `wake`.\n443:         let this = ManuallyDrop::new(self);\n444: \n445:         // SAFETY: This is safe because `Waker::from_raw` is the only way\n446:         // to initialize `wake` and `data` requiring the user to acknowledge\n447:         // that the contract of `RawWaker` is upheld.\n448:         unsafe { (this.waker.vtable.wake)(this.waker.data) };\n449:     }\n450: \n451:     /// Wakes up the task associated with this `Waker` without consuming the `Waker`.\n452:     ///\n453:     /// This is similar to [`wake()`](Self::wake), but may be slightly less efficient in\n454:     /// the case where an owned `Waker` is available. This method should be preferred to\n455:     /// calling `waker.clone().wake()`.\n456:     #[inline]\n457:     #[stable(feature = \"futures_api\", since = \"1.36.0\")]\n458:     pub fn wake_by_ref(&self) {\n459:         // The actual wakeup call is delegated through a virtual function call\n460:         // to the implementation which is defined by the executor.\n461: \n462:         // SAFETY: see `wake`\n463:         unsafe { (self.waker.vtable.wake_by_ref)(self.waker.data) }\n464:     }\n465: \n466:     /// Returns `true` if this `Waker` and another `Waker` would awake the same task.\n467:     ///\n468:     /// This function works on a best-effort basis, and may return false even\n469:     /// when the `Waker`s would awaken the same task. However, if this function\n470:     /// returns `true`, it is guaranteed that the `Waker`s will awaken the same task.\n471:     ///\n472:     /// This function is primarily used for optimization purposes — for example,\n473:     /// this type's [`clone_from`](Self::clone_from) implementation uses it to\n474:     /// avoid cloning the waker when they would wake the same task anyway.\n475:     #[inline]\n476:     #[must_use]\n477:     #[stable(feature = \"futures_api\", since = \"1.36.0\")]\n478:     pub fn will_wake(&self, other: &Waker) -> bool {\n479:         // We optimize this by comparing vtable addresses instead of vtable contents.\n480:         // This is permitted since the function is documented as best-effort.\n481:         let RawWaker { data: a_data, vtable: a_vtable } = self.waker;\n482:         let RawWaker { data: b_data, vtable: b_vtable } = other.waker;\n483:         a_data == b_data && ptr::eq(a_vtable, b_vtable)\n484:     }\n485: \n486:     /// Creates a new `Waker` from the provided `data` pointer and `vtable`.\n487:     ///\n488:     /// The `data` pointer can be used to store arbitrary data as required\n489:     /// by the executor. This could be e.g. a type-erased pointer to an `Arc`\n490:     /// that is associated with the task.\n491:     /// The value of this pointer will get passed to all functions that are part\n492:     /// of the `vtable` as the first parameter.\n493:     ///\n494:     /// It is important to consider that the `data` pointer must point to a\n495:     /// thread safe type such as an `Arc`.\n496:     ///\n497:     /// The `vtable` customizes the behavior of a `Waker`. For each operation\n498:     /// on the `Waker`, the associated function in the `vtable` will be called.\n499:     ///\n500:     /// # Safety\n501:     ///\n502:     /// The behavior of the returned `Waker` is undefined if the contract defined\n503:     /// in [`RawWakerVTable`]'s documentation is not upheld.\n504:     ///\n505:     /// (Authors wishing to avoid unsafe code may implement the [`Wake`] trait instead, at the\n506:     /// cost of a required heap allocation.)\n507:     ///\n508:     /// [`Wake`]: ../../alloc/task/trait.Wake.html\n509:     #[inline]\n510:     #[must_use]\n511:     #[stable(feature = \"waker_getters\", since = \"1.83.0\")]\n512:     #[rustc_const_stable(feature = \"waker_getters\", since = \"1.83.0\")]\n513:     pub const unsafe fn new(data: *const (), vtable: &'static RawWakerVTable) -> Self {\n514:         Waker { waker: RawWaker { data, vtable } }\n515:     }\n516: \n517:     /// Creates a new `Waker` from [`RawWaker`].\n518:     ///\n519:     /// # Safety\n520:     ///\n521:     /// The behavior of the returned `Waker` is undefined if the contract defined\n522:     /// in [`RawWaker`]'s and [`RawWakerVTable`]'s documentation is not upheld.\n523:     ///\n524:     /// (Authors wishing to avoid unsafe code may implement the [`Wake`] trait instead, at the\n525:     /// cost of a required heap allocation.)\n526:     ///\n527:     /// [`Wake`]: ../../alloc/task/trait.Wake.html\n528:     #[inline]\n529:     #[must_use]\n530:     #[stable(feature = \"futures_api\", since = \"1.36.0\")]\n531:     #[rustc_const_stable(feature = \"const_waker\", since = \"1.82.0\")]\n532:     pub const unsafe fn from_raw(waker: RawWaker) -> Waker {\n533:         Waker { waker }\n534:     }\n535: \n536:     /// Returns a reference to a `Waker` that does nothing when used.\n537:     ///\n538:     // Note!  Much of the documentation for this method is duplicated\n539:     // in the docs for `LocalWaker::noop`.\n540:     // If you edit it, consider editing the other copy too.\n541:     //\n542:     /// the waker if `self` is already the same waker.\n627:     ///\n628:     /// # Examples\n629:     ///\n630:     /// ```\n631:     /// use std::future::Future;\n632:     /// use std::pin::Pin;\n633: fmt::Debug for Waker {\n680:     fn fmt(&self, f: &mut fmt::Formatter<'_>) -> fmt::Result {\n681:         let vtable_ptr = self.waker.vtable as *const RawWakerVTable;\n682: `LocalWaker` is analogous to a [`Waker`], but it does not implement [`Send`] or [`Sync`].\n690: ///\n691: /// This handle encapsulates a [`RawWaker`] instance, which defines the\n692: /// executor-specific wakeup behavior.\n693: ///\n694: /// Local wakers can be requested from a `Context` with the [`local_waker`] method.\n695: ///\n696: /// The typical life of a `LocalWaker` is that it is constructed by an executor, wrapped in a\n697: /// [`Context`] using [`ContextBuilder`], then passed to [`Future::poll()`]. Then, if the future chooses to return\n698: /// [`Poll::Pending`], it must also store the waker somehow and call [`LocalWaker::wake()`] when\n699: /// the future should be polled again.\n700: ///\n701: /// Implements [`Clone`], but neither [`Send`] nor [`Sync`]; therefore, a local waker may\n702: /// not be moved to other threads. In general, when deciding to use wakers or local wakers,\n703: /// local wakers are preferable unless the waker needs to be sent across threads. This is because\n704: /// wakers can incur in additional cost related to memory synchronization.\n705: ///\n706: /// Note that it is preferable to use `local_waker.clone_from(&new_waker)` instead\n707: /// of `*local_waker = new_waker.clone()`, as the former will avoid cloning the waker\n708: /// unnecessarily if the two wakers [wake the same task](Self::will_wake).\n709: ///\n710: /// # Examples\n711: /// Usage of a local waker to implement a future analogous to `std::thread::yield_now()`.\n712: /// ```\n713: /// #![feature(local_waker)]\n714: /// use std::future::{Future, poll_fn};\n715: /// use std::task::Poll;\n716: ///\n717: /// // a future that returns pending once.\n718: /// fn yield_now() -> impl Future<Output=()> + Unpin {\n719: ///     let mut yielded = false;\n720: ///     poll_fn(move |cx| {\n721: ///         if !yielded {\n722: ///             yielded = true;\n723: ///             cx.local_waker().wake_by_ref();\n724: ///             return Poll::Pending;\n725: ///         }\n726: ///         return Poll::Ready(())\n727: ///     })\n728: /// }\n729: ///\n730: /// # async fn __() {\n731: /// yield_now().await;\n732: /// # }\n733: /// ```\n734: ///\n735: /// [`Future::poll()`]: core::future::Future::poll\n736: /// [`Poll::Pending`]: core::task::Poll::Pending\n737: /// [`local_waker`]: core::task::Context::local_waker\n738: #[unstable(feature = \"local_waker\", issue = \"118959\")]\n739: #[repr(transparent)]\n740: pub struct LocalWaker {\n741:     waker: RawWaker,\n742: }\n743: \n744: #[unstable(feature = \"local_waker\", issue = \"118959\")]\n745: impl Unpin for LocalWaker {}\n746: \n747: impl LocalWaker {\n748:     /// Wakes up the task associated with this `LocalWaker`.\n749:     ///\n750:     /// As long as the executor keeps running and the task is not finished, it is\n751:     /// guaranteed that each invocation of [`wake()`](Self::wake) (or\n752:     /// [`wake_by_ref()`](Self::wake_by_ref)) will be followed by at least one\n753:     /// [`poll()`] of the task to which this `LocalWaker` belongs. This makes\n754:     /// it possible to temporarily yield to other tasks while running potentially\n755:     /// unbounded processing loops.\n756:     ///\n757:     /// Note that the above implies that multiple wake-ups may be coalesced into a\n758:     /// single [`poll()`] invocation by the runtime.\n759:     ///\n760:     /// Also note that yielding to competing tasks is not guaranteed: it is the\n761:     /// executor’s choice which task to run and the executor may choose to run the\n762:     /// current task again.\n763:     ///\n764:     /// [`poll()`]: crate::future::Future::poll\n765:     #[inline]\n766:     #[unstable(feature = \"local_waker\", issue = \"118959\")]\n767:     pub fn wake(self) {\n768:         // The actual wakeup call is delegated through a virtual function call\n769:         // to the implementation which is defined by the executor.\n770: \n771:         // Don't call `drop` -- the waker will be consumed by `wake`.\n772:         let this = ManuallyDrop::new(self);\n773: \n774:         // SAFETY: This is safe because `Waker::from_raw` is the only way\n775:         // to initialize `wake` and `data` requiring the user to acknowledge\n776:         // that the contract of `RawWaker` is upheld.\n777:         unsafe { (this.waker.vtable.wake)(this.waker.data) };\n778:     }\n779: \n780:     /// Wakes up the task associated with this `LocalWaker` without consuming the `LocalWaker`.\n781:     ///\n782:     /// This is similar to [`wake()`](Self::wake), but may be slightly less efficient in\n783:     /// the case where an owned `Waker` is available. If it is known ahead of time that a call to\n94:     /// `poll` may end up taking a while, the work should be offloaded to a\n95:     /// thread pool (or something similar) to ensure that `poll` can return\n96:     /// quickly.\n97:     ///\n98:     /// # Panics\n99:     ///\n100:     /// Once a future has completed (returned `Ready` from `poll`), calling its\n101:     /// `poll` method again may panic, block forever, or cause other kinds of\n102:     /// problems; the `Future` trait places no requirements on the effects of\n103:     /// such a call. However, as the `poll` method is not marked `unsafe`,\n104:     /// Rust's usual rules apply: calls must never cause undefined behavior\n105:     /// (memory corruption, incorrect use of `unsafe` functions, or the like),\n106:     /// regardless of the future's state.\n107:     ///\n108:     /// [`Poll::Ready(val)`]: Poll::Ready\n109:     /// [`Waker`]: crate::task::Waker\n110:     /// [`Waker::wake`]: crate::task::Waker::wake\n111:     #[lang = \"poll\"]\n112:     #[stable(feature = \"futures_api\", since = \"1.36.0\")]\n113:     fn poll(self: Pin<&mut Self>, cx: &mut Context<'_>) -> Poll<Self::Output>;\n114: }\n115: \n116: #[stable(feature = \"futures_api\", since = \"1.36.0\")]\n117: impl<F: ?Sized + Future + Unpin> Future for &mut F {\n118:     type Output = F::Output;\n119: \n120:     fn poll(mut self: Pin<&mut Self>, cx: &mut Context<'_>) -> Poll<Self::Output> {\n121:         F::poll(Pin::new(&mut **self), cx)\n122:     }\n123: }\n124: \n125: #[stable(feature = \"futures_api\", since = \"1.36.0\")]\n126: impl<P> Future for Pin<P>\n127: where\n128:     P: ops::DerefMut<Target: Future>,\n129: {\n130:     type Output = <<P as ops::Deref>::Target as Future>::Output;\n131: \n132:     fn poll(self: Pin<&mut Self>, cx: &mut Context<'_>) -> Poll<Self::Output> {\n133:         <P::Target as Future>::poll(self.as_deref_mut(), cx)\n134:     }\n135: }\n136: ","url":"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-evals/rust--01f6ddf7@525258043d7f9dcc1b69d9abcb9bfea32826a219/-/blob/library/core/src/future/future.rs"}}}

An executor can define an\n22: /// implementation of this trait, and use that to construct a [`Waker`] to pass\n23: /// to the tasks that are executed on that executor.\n24: ///\n25: /// This trait is a memory-safe and ergonomic alternative to constructing a\n26: /// [`RawWaker`]. It supports the common executor design in which the data used\n27: /// to wake up a task is stored in an [`Arc`]. Some executors (especially\n28: /// those for embedded systems) cannot use this API, which is why [`RawWaker`]\n29: /// exists as an alternative for those systems.\n30: ///\n31: /// To construct a [`Waker`] from some type `W` implementing this trait,\n32: /// wrap it in an [`Arc<W>`](Arc) and call `Waker::from()` on that.\n33: /// It is also possible to convert to [`RawWaker`] in the same way.\n34: ///\n35: /// <!-- Ideally we'd link to the `From` impl, but rustdoc doesn't generate any page for it within\n36: ///      `alloc` because `alloc` neither defines nor re-exports `From` or `Waker`, and we can't\n37: ///      link ../../std/task/struct.Waker.html#impl-From%3CArc%3CW,+Global%3E%3E-for-Waker\n38: ///      without getting a link-checking error in CI. -->\n39: ///\n40: /// # Examples\n41: ///\n42: /// A basic `block_on` function that takes a future and runs it to completion on\n43: /// the current thread.\n44: ///\n45: /// **Note:** This example trades correctness for simplicity.
